## Section 010: User Journey Scenario
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed one generic engineer stands where the natural journey is the shared-library hardening, an engineer inherits a loosely typed domain library, enables the strict railguards and watches ambiguity surface as errors, converts boundary types to schemas and infers the contracts, replaces boolean state with discriminated unions and never checks, brands the identifier types, results the expected failures, versions the persisted shapes, and lands the ritual as the repo's merge gate
- **supporting_reason:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the journey works in dependency order, strictness first because it exposes what the later steps must fix, schemas before unions because parsed data feeds the union states, the ritual last because it locks in what the pass achieved
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the journey stalls at the strictness step most often, enabling strict mode on legacy code surfaces hundreds of errors at once, teams retreating to lax flags instead of ratcheting file by file, the first step needing incremental strategy the doctrine assumes rather than states
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: journeys through the doctrine's practice, corpus-process journeys stay in the seed lines
- **revision_decision:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to recast the scenario as the hardening pass with dependency-ordered steps and a ratchet strategy
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the journey's end state is self-enforcing, once schemas define contracts, unions model states, and the ritual gates merges, backsliding requires deliberately deleting guardrails, the pass converting reliability from vigilance into infrastructure, the doctrine's whole bet in one migration

## Section 021: Retry Backpressure Guidance
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed corpus-process bullets stand beside the doctrine's async rule and its cancellation doctrine, accept AbortSignal at async boundaries, compose deadlines rather than inventing disconnected timers, propagate cancellation downward, and the registry's closing row, timeouts without cancellation propagation are observability theater, a timer that aborts nothing measuring failure without preventing it
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the language layer owns the mechanism, signal acceptance and composition, while retry policy belongs to the backend companion, this doctrine ensuring every async function can participate in cancellation so the deployment layers have something to propagate through
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the erosion path is the disconnected timer, a setTimeout that rejects a promise while the underlying work continues, the visible symptom handled and the resource leak preserved, theater in exactly the registry's sense

## Section 022: Observability Checklist
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?

## Section 024: Scale Boundary Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed the seed's distributed-execution paragraphs stand while the doctrine's scale limits go unnamed, the patterns govern one repository's TypeScript, cross-repo contract synchronization exceeds the baseline, cross-service runtime concerns belong to the backend companion, organizational standards adoption exceeds any single document, and the doctrine's browser patterns assume one client codebase, not a fleet of embedded contexts
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the doctrine's enforcement engine is one compiler invocation over one project graph, its guarantees end where the compiler's visibility ends, published packages, other repos, and wire boundaries all being horizons the type system cannot see across
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the characteristic overreach is trusting types across the publish boundary, a library's exported types describe its interface without constraining its consumers' runtime data, cross-package type sharing being documentation, not enforcement, the same costume risk at ecosystem scale
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: scale limits of the doctrine, corpus-execution splitting stays in the seed paragraphs
- **revision_decision:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to state the four boundaries, single-repo enforcement, companion-owned runtime scale, standards adoption beyond documents, and the publish horizon
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the doctrine scales down perfectly and up socially, one file benefits from strict flags as much as a monorepo, while scaling up past the repo requires converting the doctrine into team standards, ratchet ledgers, and gates, the patterns staying constant while the enforcement mechanism changes from compiler to culture
